      62                 :            : 
      63                 :            : /*
      64                 :            :  * MppGroupPrep represents a strategy by which to precondition the
      65                 :            :  * argument to  a parallel aggregation plan.
      66                 :            :  *
      67                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_PREP_NONE
      68                 :            :  *    Use the input plan as is.
      69                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_PREP_HASH_GROUPS
      70                 :            :  *    Redistribute the input to collocate groups.
      71                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_PREP_HASH_DISTINCT
      72                 :            :  *    Redistribute the input on the sole distinct expression used as
      73                 :            :  *    an aggregate argument.
      74                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_PREP_FOCUS_QE
      75                 :            :  *    Focus a partitioned input on the utility QE.
      76                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_PREP_FOCUS_QD
      77                 :            :  *    Focus a partitioned input on the QD.
      78                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_PREP_BROADCAST
      79                 :            :  *    Broadcast to convert a partitioned input into a replicated one.
      80                 :            :  */
      81                 :            : typedef enum MppGroupPrep
      82                 :            : {
      83                 :            :         MPP_GRP_PREP_NONE = 0,
      84                 :            :         MPP_GRP_PREP_HASH_GROUPS,
      85                 :            :         MPP_GRP_PREP_HASH_DISTINCT,
      86                 :            :         MPP_GRP_PREP_FOCUS_QE,
      87                 :            :         MPP_GRP_PREP_FOCUS_QD,
      88                 :            :         MPP_GRP_PREP_BROADCAST
      89                 :            : } MppGroupPrep;
      90                 :            : 
      91                 :            : /*
      92                 :            :  * MppGroupType represents a stategy by which to implement parallel
      93                 :            :  * aggregation on a possibly preconditioned input plan.
      94                 :            :  *
      95                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_NONE
      96                 :            :  *    No parallel plan found.
      97                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_BASEPLAN
      98                 :            :  *    Use the sequential plan as is.
      99                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_PLAIN_2STAGE,
     100                 :            :  *    Ungrouped, 2-stage aggregation.
     101                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_GROUPED_2STAGE,
     102                 :            :  *    Grouped, 2-stage aggregation.
     103                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_PLAIN_DQA_2STAGE,
     104                 :            :  *    Ungrouped, 2-stage aggregation.
     105                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_GROUPED_DQA_2STAGE,
     106                 :            :  *    Grouped, 2-stage aggregation.
     107                 :            :  *
     108                 :            :  * TODO: Add types for min-max optimization, when ready:
     109                 :            :  *
     110                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_MINMAX
     111                 :            :  *    Use the sequential min-max optimization plan as is.
     112                 :            :  * MPP_GRP_TYPE_MINMAX_2STAGE
     113                 :            :  *    Use a 2-stage variant of min-max aggregation.
     114                 :            :  */
     115                 :            : typedef enum MppGroupType
     116                 :            : {
     117                 :            :         MPP_GRP_TYPE_NONE = 0,
     118                 :            :         MPP_GRP_TYPE_BASEPLAN,
     119                 :            :         MPP_GRP_TYPE_PLAIN_2STAGE,
     120                 :            :         MPP_GRP_TYPE_GROUPED_2STAGE,
     121                 :            :         MPP_GRP_TYPE_PLAIN_DQA_2STAGE,
     122                 :            :         MPP_GRP_TYPE_GROUPED_DQA_2STAGE,
     123                 :            : } MppGroupType;
     124                 :            : 
     125                 :            : 
     126                 :            : /* Summary values detailing the post-Motion part of a coplan for
     127                 :            :  * three-phase aggreation.  The code is as follows:
     128                 :            :  *      S = Sort
     129                 :            :  *      G = GroupAgg
     130                 :            :  *      H = HashAgg
     131                 :            :  *      P = PlainAgg
     132                 :            :  *
     133                 :            :  * So GSH means (GroupAgg (Sort (HashAgg X))).
     134                 :            :  */

     447                 :            : /*
     448                 :            :  * Function: cdb_grouping_planner
     449                 :            :  *
     450                 :            :  * This is basically an extension of the function grouping_planner() from
     451                 :            :  * planner.c.  It (conditionally) replaces the logic in the "normal case"
     452                 :            :  * (the aggregation/grouping branch) of the main "if" statement.
     453                 :            :  *
     454                 :            :  * The result is a Plan for one-, two-, or three-phase grouping/aggregation
     455                 :            :  * (possibly including a top-level join in case of DQA pruning) or NULL.
     456                 :            :  *
     457                 :            :  * A NULL result means that the ordinary sequential planner will produce
     458                 :            :  * a correct (and preferred) result, so the "normal case" code should  be
     459                 :            :  * used.
     460                 :            :  *
     461                 :            :  * A non-NULL result is taken as a partially formed Plan to be processed
     462                 :            :  * by the trailing sort/distinct/limit logic of grouping_planner().  In
     463                 :            :  * otherwords, after any associated changes to the local environment (see
     464                 :            :  * the calling code), the resulting plan should be treated as if from the
     465                 :            :  * "normal case" or the function optimize_minmax_aggregates().

    1592                 :            : 
    1593                 :            : 
    1594                 :            : /*
    1595                 :            :  * Function make_three_stage_agg_plan
    1596                 :            :  *
    1597                 :            :  * Construct a three-stage aggregation plan involving DQAs (DISTINCT-qualified
    1598                 :            :  * aggregate functions. 
    1599                 :            :  * 
    1600                 :            :  * Such a plan will always involve the following three aggregation phases: 
    1601                 :            :  *
    1602                 :            :  * - preliminary -- remove duplicate (grouping key, DQA argument) values 
    1603                 :            :  *   from an arbitrarily partitioned input; pre-aggregate plain aggregate 
    1604                 :            :  *   functions.
    1605                 :            :  *
    1606                 :            :  * - intermediate -- remove duplicate (grouping key, DQA argument) values 
    1607                 :            :  *   from an input partitioned on the grouping key; pre-aggregate the
    1608                 :            :  *   pre-aggregated results of preliminary plain aggregate functions.
    1609                 :            :  *
    1610                 :            :  * - final -- apply ordinary aggregation to DQA arguments (now distinct
    1611                 :            :  *   within their group) and final aggregation to the pre-aggregated results
    1612                 :            :  *   of the previous phase.
    1613                 :            :  *
    1614                 :            :  * In addition, if there is more than one DQA in the query, the plan will
    1615                 :            :  * join the results of the individual three-phase aggregations into the
    1616                 :            :  * final result.
    1617                 :            :  *
    1618                 :            :  * The preliminary aggregation phase occurs prior to the collocating
    1619                 :            :  * motion and is planned independently on the theory that any ordering
    1620                 :            :  * will be disrupted by the motion.  There are cases where this isn't 
    1621                 :            :  * necessarily the case, but they are unexploited for now.
    1622                 :            :  *
    1623                 :            :  * The intermediate and final aggregation phases...
    1624                 :            :  */
    1625                 :            : static Plan *
    1626                 :            : make_three_stage_agg_plan(PlannerInfo *root, MppGroupContext *ctx)
    1627                 :            : {
    1628                 :            :         Plan       *result_plan;
    1629                 :            :         QualCost        tlist_cost;
    1630                 :          0 :         Path       *path = ctx->best_path; /* no use for ctx->cheapest_path */
    1631                 :            : 
    1632                 :            :         /* We assume that we are called only when

    2494                 :            : /*

    2496                 :            :  *
    2497                 :            :  * The input to the "lower" Agg node will use a "flattened" tlist (having

    2514                 :            :  *   resno's) in the target list delivered through pointers pnum_dqas and

    2517                 :            :  *   list.

    4819                 :            : 
    4820                 :            : /* set_coplan_strategies
    4821                 :            :  *
    4822                 :            :  * Determine and cache in the given DqaInfo structure the cheapest
    4823                 :            :  * strategy that computes the answer and the cheapest strategy that 
    4824                 :            :  * computes the answer in grouping key order.
    4825                 :            :  *
    4826                 :            :  * Below, the result cardinalities are shown as <-n- where
    4827                 :            :  *
    4828                 :            :  *   x (input_rows) is the input cardinality which is usually about 
    4829                 :            :  *     equal to #segments * #distinct(grouping key, DQA arg)
    4830                 :            :  *
    4831                 :            :  *   d (darg_rows) is #distinct(grouping key, DQA arg)
    4832                 :            :  *
    4833                 :            :  *   g (group_rows) is #distinct(grouping key)
    4834                 :            :  *
    4835                 :            :  * The coplan through the Motion that collocates tuples on the
    4836                 :            :  * grouping key is planned independently and will be one of
    4837                 :            :  *
    4838                 :            :  *    <- Motion <-x- HashAgg <-t- R
    4839                 :            :  *    <- Motion <-x- GroupAgg <- Sort <-t- R
    4840                 :            :  *
    4841                 :            :  * which is encoded in DqaInfo by the flag use_hashed_preliminary.
    4842                 :            :  *
    4843                 :            :  * The possible post-Motion strategies are encoded as enum values of 
    4844                 :            :  * type DqaCoplanType and indicate all the required plan nodes.
    4845                 :            :  *
    4846                 :            :  * Vector aggregation strategies that produce a result ordered on the
    4847                 :            :  * grouping key are:
    4848                 :            :  *
    4849                 :            :  * DQACOPLAN_GGS:       <-g- GroupAgg <-d- GroupAgg <- Sort <-x-
    4850                 :            :  * DQACOPLAN_GSH:       <-g- GroupAgg <- Sort <-d- HashAgg <-x-
    4851                 :            :  * DQACOPLAN_SHH:       <- Sort <-g-  HashAgg <-d- HashAgg <-x-
    4852                 :            :  * 
    4853                 :            :  * In addition, the vector aggreagation strategy
    4854                 :            :  *
    4855                 :            :  * DQACOPLAN_HH:        <-g- HashAgg <-d- HashAgg <-x- R
    4856                 :            :  *
    4857                 :            :  * produces an unordered result.
    4858                 :            :  *
    4859                 :            :  * Scalar aggregation strategies are:
    4860                 :            :  *
    4861                 :            :  * DQACOPLAN_PGS:       <-1- PlainAgg <-d- GroupAgg <- Sort <-x- R
    4862                 :            :  * DQACOPLAN_PH:        <-1- PlainAgg <-d- HashedAgg <-x- R
    4863                 :            :  *
    4864                 :            :  */

    5369                 :            : /*
    5370                 :            :  * deconstruct_within_agg
    5371                 :            :  *   deconstruct within-aggregate and normal aggregate expressions to sub pieces.
    5372                 :            :  *
    5373                 :            :  * In the split-DQA-join pattern, we want to deconstruct individual aggregate
    5374                 :            :  * or percentile expressions, group them, and relocate them to the appropriate
    5375                 :            :  * sub-plan target list.  The information about which expression goes to which
    5376                 :            :  * sub-plan is stored in MppGroupContext structure, and the function returns
    5377                 :            :  * Var that points to the expression on sub-plan which the original expression
    5378                 :            :  * is replaced with.
    5379                 :            :  *

    6395                 :            : 
    6396                 :            : /*
    6397                 :            :  * plan_within_agg_persort
    6398                 :            :  *   Make a series of plans to calculate percentile per identical sort clause.
    6399                 :            :  *
    6400                 :            :  * The main stream of this planner is:
    6401                 :            :  *  - Build the base plan
    6402                 :            :  *  - Sort the input by group and target value
    6403                 :            :  *  - Split the input into two
    6404                 :            :  *  - One for the outer
    6405                 :            :  *  - The other for the inner, aggregate to count actual row number
    6406                 :            :  *  - Join two trees to get the inner row count to the sorted outer together
    6407                 :            :  *  - Aggregate the result of join to perform the final aggregate
    6408                 :            :  *
    6409                 :            :  * The first step is to figure out if we could optimize the input by
    6410                 :            :  * de-duplicate table.  If so, we create a sub-plan with aggregate to
    6411                 :            :  * reduce the rows into GROUP + ORDER unit and add the peer count in this unit.
    6412                 :            :  * If we don't take de-duplicate plan, we append constant 1 as the peer count
    6413                 :            :  * to the target list to match the semantics with de-duplicate plan.  In any
    6414                 :            :  * case, the input plan is wrapped by a SubqueryScan in order not to confuse
    6415                 :            :  * upper plan.  The peer count takes account into NULL, so that the percentile
    6416                 :            :  * function can operate on only non-NULL target value.
    6417                 :            :  *
    6418                 :            :  * The next step is for the outer plan; sort the input tuples by group clause
    6419                 :            :  * and the target value.  During this process, the input tuples are distributed
    6420                 :            :  * by the group clause.  We need to keep this order until the final aggregate
    6421                 :            :  * so that the final percentile function can tell ordering of the input.
    6422                 :            :  *
    6423                 :            :  * Then we look at the inner side.  It basically calculates number of rows
    6424                 :            :  * per group.  Since we know the peer count per each distinct target value in
    6425                 :            :  * a group in either of naive or deduplicate approach, we actually take sum()
    6426                 :            :  * rather than count() to calculate the total number of non-NULL target values.
    6427                 :            :  *
    6428                 :            :  * Now, we can join two plans.  The inner total count is going to be with
    6429                 :            :  * the target value for each group here.  Note that we use Merge Join to
    6430                 :            :  * keep the outer order and the inner should have capability to be rescanned
    6431                 :            :  * per its requirement.
    6432                 :            :  *
    6433                 :            :  * Finally, the rows are aggregated per group.  Since PercentileExpr needs
    6434                 :            :  * to know the peer count and the total count in conjunction with its
    6435                 :            :  * original argument and the target value (as the ORDER BY clause,) and we now
    6436                 :            :  * know where those values are, here we attach those expressions to
    6437                 :            :  * PercentileExpr nodes.  These additional expressions are similar to
    6438                 :            :  * AggOrder in Aggref, which will be combined with the original argument
    6439                 :            :  * expression in the executor to be evaluated.
    6440                 :            :  *
    6441                 :            :  * The final result of this function is a plan ending Agg node with target
    6442                 :            :  * list including each percentile result.  Note this function should not
    6443                 :            :  * change the semantics of input target list as an encapsulation.
    6444                 :            :  */
    6445                 :            : static Plan *
    6446                 :            : plan_within_agg_persort(PlannerInfo *root,
    6447                 :            :                                                 GroupContext *group_context,
    6448                 :            :                                                 List *sortClause,
    6449                 :            :                                                 List *current_pathkeys,
    6450                 :            :                                                 Plan *result_plan)
    6451                 :            : {
    6452                 :            :         WithinAggContext        wag_context;
    6453                 :            :         Plan                       *outer_plan, *inner_plan;
    6454                 :            :         List                       *partners;
    6455                 :            :         ListCell                   *l;
    6456                 :            : 
    6457                 :          0 :         memset(&wag_context, 0, sizeof(WithinAggContext));
    6458                 :          0 :         wag_context.current_pathkeys = current_pathkeys;
    6459                 :            : 
    6460                 :            :         /*
    6461                 :            :          * Group clause expressions should be in ascending order,
    6462                 :            :          * because our MergeJoin is not able to handle descending-ordered
    6463                 :            :          * child plans.  It is desirable to improve MergeJoin, but it requires
    6464                 :            :          * amount of work.
    6465                 :            :          */
    6466         [ #  # ]:          0 :         foreach (l, root->parse->groupClause)
    6467                 :            :         {
    6468                 :          0 :                 GroupClause        *gc = lfirst(l);

    6534                 :            :                                                                                 &wag_context,
    6535                 :          0 :                                                                                 outer_plan,
    6536                 :          0 :                                                                                 inner_plan);
    6537                 :            : 
    6538                 :            : #ifdef NOT_USED
    6539                 :            : if (true)
    6540                 :            : {

    6566                 :            : 
    6567                 :            : /*
    6568                 :            :  * within_agg_planner
    6569                 :            :  *
    6570                 :            :  * This is the entry point of within-aggregate planner.
    6571                 :            :  * Makes a specialized plan for within aggregates.  If we find the query
    6572                 :            :  * has normal aggregates among the within-aggregates, or within-aggregates
    6573                 :            :  * have different sortClause, we generate multiple sub-plans regarding with
    6574                 :            :  * the sortClause and combine the results by joining those sub-plan trees.
    6575                 :            :  * For the normal aggregates, we call cdb_grouping_planner() to plan the tree,
    6576                 :            :  * and treat it as one of the split sub-plans.
    6577                 :            :  */
    6578                 :            : Plan *
    6579                 :            : within_agg_planner(PlannerInfo *root,
    6580                 :            :                                    AggClauseCounts *agg_counts,
    6581                 :            :                                    GroupContext *group_context)
    6582                 :            : {
    6583                 :            :         List       *aggnodes, *percnodes;
    6584                 :            :         ListCell   *l;
    6585                 :            :         List      **aggreflist;
    6586                 :            :         List      **sortlist;
    6587                 :            :         int                     numsortlist;
    6588                 :            :         int                     numGroupCols, numDistinctCols;
    6589                 :            :         AttrNumber *grpColIdx;
    6590                 :            :         Oid                *grpOperators;
    6591                 :            :         AttrNumber *distinctColIdx;
    6592                 :            :         int                     i;
    6593                 :            :         List       *sub_tlist;
    6594                 :            :         AttrNumber      next_resno;
    6595                 :            :         List       *current_pathkeys;
    6596                 :            :         Plan       *result_plan;
    6597                 :            : 
    6598                 :          0 :         aggnodes = extract_nodes(NULL, (Node *) root->parse->targetList, T_Aggref);
    6599                 :          0 :         aggnodes = list_concat(aggnodes,
    6600                 :          0 :                                                    extract_nodes(NULL, (Node *) root->parse->havingQual, T_Aggref));
    6601                 :          0 :         aggnodes = list_concat(aggnodes,
    6602                 :          0 :                                                    extract_nodes(NULL, (Node *) root->parse->scatterClause, T_Aggref));
    6603                 :          0 :         percnodes = extract_nodes(NULL, (Node *) root->parse->targetList, T_PercentileExpr);
    6604                 :          0 :         percnodes = list_concat(percnodes,
    6605                 :          0 :                                                         extract_nodes(NULL, (Node *) root->parse->havingQual, T_PercentileExpr));
    6606                 :          0 :         percnodes = list_concat(percnodes,
    6607                 :          0 :                                                         extract_nodes(NULL, (Node *) root->parse->scatterClause, T_PercentileExpr));
    6608                 :            :         /* Allocate maximum number of list */
    6609                 :          0 :         numsortlist = list_length(percnodes) + 1;
    6610                 :            :         /* initialize each element with NIL */
    6611                 :          0 :         aggreflist = (List **) palloc0(sizeof(List *) * numsortlist);

    6613                 :          0 :         numsortlist = 0; /* Use this as a counter */
